style="padding-right:0.5em;">\n<div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Number of employees</div>\n</th>\n<td style="line-height:1.35em;">19,794<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ar2015_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-ar2015-2">[2]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.5em;">Website</th>\n<td style="line-height:1.35em;"><a class="external text" href="http://www.hydroquebec.com/en/" rel="nofollow">www.hydroquebec.com</a></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p><b>Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Public_utility" title="Public utility">public utility</a> that manages the <a href="/wiki/Electricity_generation" title="Electricity generation">generation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_power_transmission" title="Electric power transmission">transmission</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electricity_distribution" title="Electricity distribution">distribution</a> of <a href="/wiki/Electricity" title="Electricity">electricity</a> in <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>.</p>\n<p>It was formed by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Quebec" title="Government of Quebec">Government of Quebec</a> in 1944 from the expropriation of private firms. This was followed by massive investment in hydro-electric projects like <a href="/wiki/Churchill_Falls_Generating_Station" title="Churchill Falls Generating Station">Churchill Falls</a> and the <a href="/wiki/James_Bay_Project" title="James Bay Project">James Bay Project</a>. Today, with 63 <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectric</a> <a href="/wiki/Power_station" title="Power station">power stations</a>, the combined output capacity is 36,912 megawatts. Extra power is exported from the province and Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec supplies 10 per cent of <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a>\'s power requirements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-3">[3]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec is a <a href="/wiki/State-owned_enterprise" title="State-owned enterprise">state-owned enterprise</a> based in <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>. In 2015, it paid CAD$2.36 billion in <a href="/wiki/Dividend" title="Dividend">dividends</a> to its sole <a href="/wiki/Shareholder" title="Shareholder">shareholder</a>, the Government of Qu\xc3\xa9bec. Its residential power rates are among the lowest in North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-4">[4]</a></sup></p>\n<p>More than 40 percent of Canada\xe2\x80\x99s water resources are in Qu\xc3\xa9bec and Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec is the fourth largest hydropower producer in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-3">[3]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The company logo, a stylized "Q" fashioned out of a circle and a lightning bolt, was designed by Montreal-based design agency Gagnon/Valkus in 1960.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>\n<p></p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc">\n<div class="toctitle">\n<h2>Contents</h2>\n</div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MLH_%26_P_-_monteurs_de_ligne.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<i>Montreal Light, Heat and Power</i> linemen.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h3><span id="1945\xe2\x80\x931959:_beginnings_and_development"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1945.E2.80.931959:_beginnings_and_development">1945\xe2\x80\x931959: beginnings and development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1945\xe2\x80\x931959: beginnings and development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In Quebec, advocates for the creation of a public hydroelectric utility protested against high costs, poor <a href="/wiki/Rural_electrification" title="Rural electrification">rural electrification</a>, and the lack of French speakers in management positions in hydroelectricity companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-6">[6]</a></sup> In 1944, <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Light,_Heat_%26_Power" title="Montreal Light, Heat &amp; Power">Montreal Light, Heat &amp; Power</a> company was nationalised, along with its subsidiary, Beauharnois Power, and Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec was created to manage the companies.</p>\n<p>Quebec Premier <a href="/wiki/Ad%C3%A9lard_Godbout" title="Ad\xc3\xa9lard Godbout">Ad\xc3\xa9lard Godbout</a> adopted a policy of investing 10 million dollars per year in rural electrification.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-6">[6]</a></sup> However, in 1944 the government changed, and the new premier <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Duplessis" title="Maurice Duplessis">Maurice Duplessis</a> was opposed to any form of government intervention in the economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Local cooperatives were created to bring power to rural areas. Duplessis remained in power until 1960, and during that time there were no further nationalisations of companies, and Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec mostly served the Montreal area.</p>\n<p>Major projects included:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bersimis-1_generating_station" title="Bersimis-1 generating station">Bersimis-1 generating station</a> completed in 1956, 1,125 MW</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bersimis-2_generating_station" title="Bersimis-2 generating station">Bersimis-2 generating station</a> completed in 1959, 845 MW</li>\n<li>the <a href="/wiki/Beauharnois_Hydroelectric_Generating_Station" title="Beauharnois Hydroelectric Generating Station">Beauharnois Hydroelectric Generating Station</a> completed in 1961, 1,903 MW.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Carillon_Generating_Station" title="Carillon Generating Station">Carillon Generating Station</a> built 1959-1964, 752 MW</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Between 1944 and 1962, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec\'s installed capacity increased from 616 to 3,661 MW<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> while lowering residential power rates by half in the Montreal area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span id="1960\xe2\x80\x931979:_the_second_nationalisation"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1960.E2.80.931979:_the_second_nationalisation">1960\xe2\x80\x931979: the second nationalisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1960\xe2\x80\x931979: the second nationalisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%C3%89vacuateur_de_crues_R-B.jpg"><img alt="A giant staircase dug in solid rock in the wilderness." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/%C3%89vacuateur_de_crues_R-B.jpg/240px-%C3%89vacuateur_de_crues_R-B.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/%C3%89vacuateur_de_crues_R-B.jpg/360px-%C3%89vacuateur_de_crues_R-B.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/%C3%89vacuateur_de_crues_R-B.jpg/480px-%C3%89vacuateur_de_crues_R-B.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%C3%89vacuateur_de_crues_R-B.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe spillway at the <a href="/wiki/Robert-Bourassa_generating_station" title="Robert-Bourassa generating station">Robert-Bourassa generating station</a> can deal with a water flow twice as large as the Saint Lawrence River.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETurgeon1992110_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETurgeon1992110-10">[10]</a></sup> Inaugurated in 1979 the 5,616 MW generating station was at the heart of a network of 8 hydroelectric stations known as the <a href="/wiki/James_Bay_Project" title="James Bay Project">James Bay Project</a>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Duplessis\' conservative reign, now known as the <a href="/wiki/Grande_Noirceur" title="Grande Noirceur">Grande Noirceur</a>, ended when he died in office in 1959. The subsequent election of the <a href="/wiki/Quebec_Liberal_Party" title="Quebec Liberal Party">Quebec Liberal Party</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Jean_Lesage" title="Jean Lesage">Jean Lesage</a>, marked the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Quiet_Revolution" title="Quiet Revolution">Quiet Revolution</a>, a period of reform and modernisation. The new government gave Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec an exclusive mandate to develop new sites. In 1963 the government authorized it to acquire private electricity distributors, including the <a href="/wiki/Gatineau_Power_Company" title="Gatineau Power Company">Gatineau Power Company</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Shawinigan_Water_%26_Power_Company" title="Shawinigan Water &amp; Power Company">Shawinigan Water &amp; Power Company</a> Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec achieved province-wide scope.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> All of the 46 rural coops accepted Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec\xe2\x80\x99s 1963 buyout offer, except Saint-Jean-Baptiste-de-Rouville which still exists. Major projects during this period included:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Manic-Outardes Project, a 7-dam hydroelectric complex including the <a href="/wiki/Jean-Lesage_generating_station" title="Jean-Lesage generating station">Jean-Lesage generating station</a> (1,145 MW), <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9-L%C3%A9vesque_generating_station" title="Ren\xc3\xa9-L\xc3\xa9vesque generating station">Ren\xc3\xa9-L\xc3\xa9vesque generating station</a> (1,244 MW), and the <a href="/wiki/Daniel-Johnson_Dam" title="Daniel-Johnson Dam">Daniel-Johnson Dam</a> (2,596 MW), originally named Manic-2, Manic-3, and Manic-5 respectively. Because these stations were 700 kilometres away from the urban centers in southern Quebec, power was stepped up to <span class="nowrap">735 kV</span>, a world first, led by engineer <a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Archambault" title="Jean-Jacques Archambault">Jean-Jacques Archambault</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Churchill_Falls_Generating_Station" title="Churchill Falls Generating Station">Churchill Falls Generating Station</a>, 5,428 MW. The station is in <a href="/wiki/Labrador" title="Labrador">Labrador</a> and the government of Quebec refused to allow power to be transferred through Quebec,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> forcing the negotiation of a contract where Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec buys power from the project at 1969 prices until the year 2041.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Phase I of the <a href="/wiki/James_Bay_Project" title="James Bay Project">James Bay Project</a>.</li>\n<li>Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec worked with <a href="/wiki/Atomic_Energy_of_Canada_Limited" title="Atomic Energy of Canada Limited">Atomic Energy of Canada Limited</a> to build the <a href="/wiki/CANDU_reactor" title="CANDU reactor">CANDU reactor</a> equipped <a href="/wiki/Gentilly_Nuclear_Generating_Station" title="Gentilly Nuclear Generating Station">Gentilly Nuclear Generating Station</a>, which closed in 2012.</li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span id="1980\xe2\x80\x931996:_restructuring"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1980.E2.80.931996:_restructuring">1980\xe2\x80\x931996: restructuring</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1980\xe2\x80\x931996: restructuring">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Because of the economic climate, demand for electricity dropped significantly in the early 1980s, which led to structural changes at Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec. It became a <a href="/wiki/Joint-stock_company" title="Joint-stock company">joint stock company</a> whose sole shareholder is Qu\xc3\xa9bec government, to which it pays an annual dividend. It was also given the mandate to export power and to work in any energy-related field.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 1986 the <a href="/wiki/Quebec_%E2%80%93_New_England_Transmission" title="Quebec \xe2\x80\x93 New England Transmission">Quebec \xe2\x80\x93 New England Transmission</a> began bringing power from the James Bay Project 1,100 kilometers south to the Boston area.</p>\n<p>Phase II of the James Bay Project started in 1987 and took nine years to complete. Construction of the <a href="/wiki/Denis-Perron_Dam" title="Denis-Perron Dam">Denis-Perron Dam</a> began in 1994.</p>\n<h3><span id="1997\xe2\x80\x93present:_renewed_growth"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1997.E2.80.93present:_renewed_growth">1997\xe2\x80\x93present: renewed growth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1997\xe2\x80\x93present: renewed growth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the late \'90s the wholesale electricity market opened up across North America, and Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec opened its transmission system and wholesale electricity market to competition both inside and outside its tranditional service area. The U.S. <a href="/wiki/Federal_Energy_Regulatory_Commission" title="Federal Energy Regulatory Commission">Federal Energy Regulatory Commission</a> granted Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec a licence to sell wholesale electricity at market prices, enabling Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec to expand its market. Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec acquired a substantial share of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Noverco&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Noverco (page does not exist)">Noverco</a>, controller of natural gas distributor <a href="/wiki/Gaz_M%C3%A9tro" title="Gaz M\xc3\xa9tro">Gaz M\xc3\xa9tro</a>, to participate in that market in northeastern North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eastmain_map.png"><img alt="Map of the Eastmain watershed" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="254" data-file-width="396" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Eastmain_map.png/220px-Eastmain_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Eastmain_map.png/330px-Eastmain_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3f/Eastmain_map.png 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eastmain_map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nthe Rupert River diversion will channel part of the natural flow of the river (orange on the map) to the Robert-Bourassa Reservoir.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>In 2002 the <a href="/wiki/Agreement_Respecting_a_New_Relationship_Between_the_Cree_Nation_and_the_Government_of_Quebec" title="Agreement Respecting a New Relationship Between the Cree Nation and the Government of Quebec">Agreement Respecting a New Relationship Between the Cree Nation and the Government of Quebec</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Council_of_the_Crees" title="Grand Council of the Crees">Grand Council of the Crees</a> and the Quebec government made possible the development of the <a href="/wiki/Eastmain_Reservoir" title="Eastmain Reservoir">Eastmain Reservoir</a>. The 5,000 million CAD Eastmain-1-A and Sarcelle powerhouses and <a href="/wiki/Rupert_River" title="Rupert River">Rupert River</a> diversion project. This will provide water power to new turbines at Eastmain-1 or Eastmain-1-A and Sarcelle powerhouses and will provide increased flow at the existing La Grande-1 generating station as well as Robert-Bourassa or La Grande-2-A.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Output will be 918 MW.</p>\n<p>Other stations commissioned since 1997 are:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>\n<ul>\n<li>Sainte-Marguerite-3 in 2003, 882 MW.</li>\n<li>P\xc3\xa9ribonka in 2008, 385 MW.</li>\n<li>Rocher-de-Grand-M\xc3\xa8re in 2004, 230 MW.</li>\n<li>Eastmain-1 in 2007, 519 MW.</li>\n<li>Rapide-des-C\xc5\x93urs in 2009, 76 MW.</li>\n<li>Chute-Allard in 2009, 62 MW</li>\n<li>Mercier in 2009, 55 MW.</li>\n<li>Eastmain-1-A in 2012, 750 MW.</li>\n<li>La Sarcelle in 2013, 159 MW.</li>\n<li>Romaine-2 in 2014, 640 MW.</li>\n<li>Romaine-1 in 2015, 270 MW.</li>\n<li>Romaine-3 and Romaine-4 before 2020</li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_outages">Major outages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Major outages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tree_branch_after_ice_storm.JPG"><img alt="Barren tree branches covered with a thick coat of ice." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Tree_branch_after_ice_storm.JPG/180px-Tree_branch_after_ice_storm.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Tree_branch_after_ice_storm.JPG/270px-Tree_branch_after_ice_storm.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Tree_branch_after_ice_storm.JPG/360px-Tree_branch_after_ice_storm.JPG 2x" width="180"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tree_branch_after_ice_storm.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_American_ice_storm_of_1998" title="North American ice storm of 1998">North American ice storm of January 1998</a> left 1.4 million Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec customers in the dark for up to five weeks.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>In 1988, all of Quebec and parts of <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a> lost power because of an equipment failure at a substation on the <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te-Nord" title="C\xc3\xb4te-Nord">North Shore</a>. The <a href="/wiki/March_1989_geomagnetic_storm" title="March 1989 geomagnetic storm">March 1989 geomagnetic storm</a> tripped <a href="/wiki/Circuit_breaker" title="Circuit breaker">circuit breakers</a> on the transmission network causing a nine-hour Quebec-wide blackout.</p>\n<p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_American_Ice_Storm_of_1998" title="North American Ice Storm of 1998">North American ice storm of 1998</a>, five days of <a href="/wiki/Freezing_rain" title="Freezing rain">freezing rain</a> collapsed 600 kilometres (370\xc2\xa0mi) of <a href="/wiki/High_voltage" title="High voltage">high voltage</a> power lines and over 3,000 kilometres (1,900\xc2\xa0mi) of medium and <a href="/wiki/Low_voltage" title="Low voltage">low voltage</a> distribution lines in southern Quebec. Up to 1.4 million customers were without power for up to five weeks.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_structure_and_financial_results">Corporate structure and financial results</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Corporate structure and financial results">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_structure">Corporate structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Corporate structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Quebec_Map_with_Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec_infrastructures-en.png"><img alt="Map of Quebec showing the location of power stations and 450 kV and 735 kV power lines." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="991" data-file-width="1261" height="259" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Quebec_Map_with_Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec_infrastructures-en.png/330px-Quebec_Map_with_Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec_infrastructures-en.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Quebec_Map_with_Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec_infrastructures-en.png/495px-Quebec_Map_with_Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec_infrastructures-en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Quebec_Map_with_Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec_infrastructures-en.png/660px-Quebec_Map_with_Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec_infrastructures-en.png 2x" width="330"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Quebec_Map_with_Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec_infrastructures-en.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nHydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec generation and main transmission network, as of 2008.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Like its counterparts in the North American utility industry, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec was reorganized in the late 1990s to comply with electricity <a href="/wiki/Deregulation" title="Deregulation">deregulation</a> in the United States. While still a <a href="/wiki/Vertical_integration" title="Vertical integration">vertically integrated</a> company, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec has created separate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Business_unit" title="Business unit">business units</a> dealing with the <a href="/wiki/Electricity_generation" title="Electricity generation">generation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_power_transmission" title="Electric power transmission">transmission</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electricity_distribution" title="Electricity distribution">distribution</a> aspects of the business.</p>\n<p>The transmission division, <a href="/wiki/Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec%27s_electricity_transmission_system" title="Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec\'s electricity transmission system">Trans\xc3\x89nergie</a>, was the first to be spun off in 1997, in response to the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Federal_Energy_Regulatory_Commission" title="Federal Energy Regulatory Commission">Federal Energy Regulatory Commission</a>\'s publication of Order 888.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEInternational_Energy_Agency2004127_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInternational_Energy_Agency2004127-19">[19]</a></sup> The restructuring was completed in the year 2000 with the adoption of Bill 116, which amended the <i>Act respecting the R\xc3\xa9gie de l\'\xc3\xa9nergie</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> to enact the functional separation of Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec\'s various business units.</p>\n<p>This functional separation and the creation of a so-called <i>"heritage pool"</i> (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <span lang="fr" xml:lang="fr"><i>volume patrimonial</i></span>) of electricity echoed a recommendation of a <a href="/wiki/Merrill_Lynch" title="Merrill Lynch">Merrill Lynch</a> study commissioned by the <a href="/wiki/Lucien_Bouchard" title="Lucien Bouchard">Lucien Bouchard</a> government. The January 2000 report was aimed at finding a way to deregulate the electricity market in a way that was consistent with continental trends while maintaining the "Quebec social pact"; namely low, uniform and stable rates across the province, "particularly in the residential sector".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETrabandt2000_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETrabandt2000-21">[21]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Legislation passed in 2000 commits the generation division, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec Production, to provide the distribution division, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec Distribution, a yearly <i>heritage pool</i> of up to 165 TWh of energy plus ancillary services\xe2\x80\x94including an extra 13.9 TWh for losses and a guaranteed peak capacity of 34,342 MW<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>\xe2\x80\x94at a set price of 2.79\xc2\xa2 per kWh. Order in council 1277-2001 specifies quantities to be delivered for each of the 8,760 hourly intervals, which vary from 11,420 to 34,342 MW.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec Distribution has to buy the remainder of the power and energy it needs\xe2\x80\x94approximately 8.2 TWh in 2007<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HQapprovisionnements_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-HQapprovisionnements-24">[24]</a></sup> \xe2\x80\x94 by calling for tenders for long-term contracts open to all suppliers, including Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec Production, or targeted towards suppliers of a particular energy source, like wind, gas power, biomass or small hydro.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HQContracts_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-HQContracts-25">[25]</a></sup> For instance, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec Distribution launched calls for tenders in 2003 and 2005, for 1,000 and 2,000 MW of wind power respectively. Early deliveries started in 2006 and the 23 <a href="/wiki/Wind_farm" title="Wind farm">wind farms</a> under contract should be completely on-line by December 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HQWindFarms_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-HQWindFarms-26">[26]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The Trans\xc3\x89nergie and distribution divisions remain regulated by the <i>R\xc3\xa9gie de l\'\xc3\xa9nergie du Qu\xc3\xa9bec</i> (Quebec Energy Board), an <a href="/wiki/Administrative_law" title="Administrative law">administrative tribunal</a> established to set retail rates for electricity and natural gas for residential, commercial and industrial service in the province based on a cost-of-service approach. The <i>R\xc3\xa9gie</i> also has extended powers, including approval authority over every transmission and distribution-related capital expenditure project exceeding C$10 million; approval of the terms of service and of long-term supply contracts; dealing with customer complaints; and the setting and enforcement of safety and reliability standards for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electric_grid" title="Electric grid">electric grid</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTER.C3.A9gie_de_l.27.C3.A9nergie_du_Qu.C3.A9bec20084_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTER.C3.A9gie_de_l.27.C3.A9nergie_du_Qu.C3.A9bec20084-27">[27]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The Generation division, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec Production is not subject to regulation by the <i>R\xc3\xa9gie</i>. However, it must still submit every new construction project to a full environmental impact process, including the release of extensive environmental studies. The release of the studies are followed by a public hearing process conducted by the <i>Bureau d\'audiences publiques sur l\'environnement</i>.</p>\n<p>Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec employed 23,659 people in 2009,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2011a3_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2011a3-28">[28]</a></sup> including 2,060 engineers, making the company the largest employer of engineers in Quebec.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>\n<div aria-labelledby="Main_subsidiaries_of_Hydro-Qu.C3.A9bec" class="navbox" 1]</a></sup></th>\n<td>18,834</td>\n<td>18,566</td>\n<td>18,419</td>\n<td>18,250</td>\n<td>17,206</td>\n<td>15,264</td>\n<td>17,376</td>\n<td>16,220</td>\n<td>15,128</td>\n<td>14,208</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>For the year ending on December 31, 2011, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec posted net earnings of C$2.611 billion, up 3.8% from 2010 despite lower electricity prices on export markets and the high value of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_dollar" title="Canadian dollar">Canadian dollar</a>. <a href="/wiki/Revenue" title="Revenue">Revenue</a> were down 3.8% in 2011 at C$12.392 billion, while <a href="/wiki/Cost" title="Cost">expenditures</a> amounted to C$7.284 billion, down by C$159 million from 2010, mainly due to lower short-term electricity and fuel purchases and the repeal of Quebec\'s capital tax.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012a48_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012a48-34">[33]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The company has assets of C$69.637 billion, C$56.901 billion of which are tangible assets. Its long-term debt stood at C$42.05 billion, and the company reported a capitalization rate of 31.0% in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012a50_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012a50-35">[34]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bond_(finance)" title="Bond (finance)">Bonds</a> issued by Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec are <a href="/wiki/Government_debt" title="Government debt">backed</a> by the Quebec government. On December 31, 2011, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Long-run" title="Long-run">long-term</a> <a href="/wiki/Security_(finance)" title="Security (finance)">securities</a> of Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec were rated <i>Aa2 stable</i> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moody%27s" title="Moody\'s">Moody\'s</a>, <i>AA- positive</i> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fitch_Group" title="Fitch Group">Fitch Ratings</a> and <i>A+</i> by <a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s" title="Standard &amp; Poor\'s">Standard &amp; Poor\'s</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012a52_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012a52-36">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 2011, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec paid a C$1.958 billion <a href="/wiki/Dividend" title="Dividend">dividend</a> to its sole shareholder, the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Quebec" title="Government of Quebec">Government of Quebec</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012a48_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012a48-34">[33]</a></sup> Between 2007 and 2011, the company paid a total of C$10.358 billion in dividends.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012c16_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012c16-37">[36]</a></sup> It took on $8b in debt during the same period.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Privatization_debate">Privatization debate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Privatization debate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec Building in the center." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2912" data-file-width="4368" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Montreal_skyline_with_Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec_building.jpg/280px-Montreal_skyline_with_Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec_building.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Montreal_skyline_with_Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec_building.jpg/420px-Montreal_skyline_with_Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec_building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Montreal_skyline_with_Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec_building.jpg/560px-Montreal_skyline_with_Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec_building.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Montreal_skyline_with_Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec_building.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%89difice_Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec" title="\xc3\x89difice Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec">Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec Building</a> is a landmark of Montreal\'s downtown.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>In 1981, the <a href="/wiki/Parti_Qu%C3%A9b%C3%A9cois" title="Parti Qu\xc3\xa9b\xc3\xa9cois">Parti Qu\xc3\xa9b\xc3\xa9cois</a> government redefined Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec\'s mission by modifying the terms of the <i>social pact</i> of 1944. The government issued itself 43,741,090 shares worth C$100 each,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2011a90_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2011a90-38">[37]</a></sup> and the amended statute stated that Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec would now pay up to 75% of its net earnings in dividends.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBolduc2000245_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBolduc2000245-39">[38]</a></sup> This amendment to the <i>Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec Act</i> started an episodic debate on whether Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec should be fully or partially privatized. In recent years, economist Marcel Boyer and businessman Claude Garcia\xe2\x80\x94both associated with the conservative think tank <i>The Montreal Economic Institute</i>\xe2\x80\x94have often raised the issue, claiming that the company could be better managed by the private sector and that the proceeds from a sale would lower <a href="/wiki/Government_debt" title="Government debt">public debt</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGarcia2009_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGarcia2009-41">[40]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Without going as far as Boyer and Garcia, <a href="/wiki/Mario_Dumont" title="Mario Dumont">Mario Dumont</a>, the head of the <a href="/wiki/Action_d%C3%A9mocratique_du_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Action d\xc3\xa9mocratique du Qu\xc3\xa9bec">Action d\xc3\xa9mocratique du Qu\xc3\xa9bec</a>, briefly discussed the possibility of selling a minority stake of Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec during the <a href="/wiki/Quebec_general_election,_2008" title="Quebec general election, 2008">2008 election campaign</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9ger_Marketing" title="L\xc3\xa9ger Marketing">L\xc3\xa9ger Marketing</a> poll conducted in November 2008 found that a majority of Quebec respondents (53%) were opposed to his proposal to sell 7.5% of the company\'s <a href="/wiki/Equity_(finance)" title="Equity (finance)">equity</a> to Quebec citizens and businesses, while 38% were in favor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Commenting on the issue on <a href="/wiki/Guy_A._Lepage" title="Guy A. Lepage">Guy A. Lepage</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Talk_show" title="Talk show">talk show</a>, former PQ Premier Jacques Parizeau estimated that such an idea would be quite unpopular in public opinion, adding that Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec is often seen by Quebecers as a national success story and a source of pride.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> This could explain why various privatization proposals in the past have received little public attention. The liberal government has repeatedly stated that Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec is not for sale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Like many other economists,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> Yvan Allaire, from <a href="/wiki/HEC_Montr%C3%A9al" title="HEC Montr\xc3\xa9al">Montreal\'s Hautes \xc3\xa9tudes commerciales</a> business school, advocate increased electricity rates as a way to increase the government\'s annual dividend without resorting to privatization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> Others, like columnist Bertrand Tremblay of <a href="/wiki/Saguenay,_Quebec" title="Saguenay, Quebec">Saguenay</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Quotidien_(Saguenay)" title="Le Quotidien (Saguenay)">Le Quotidien</a></i>, claim that privatization would signal a drift to the days when Quebec\'s natural resources were sold in bulk to foreigners at ridiculously low prices. "For too long, Tremblay writes, Quebec was somewhat of a banana republic, almost giving away its forestry and water resources. In turn, those foreign interests were exporting our jobs associated with the development of our natural resources with the complicity of local vultures".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Left-wing academics, such as <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_du_Qu%C3%A9bec_%C3%A0_Montr%C3%A9al" title="Universit\xc3\xa9 du Qu\xc3\xa9bec \xc3\xa0 Montr\xc3\xa9al">UQAM</a>\'s L\xc3\xa9o-Paul Lauzon and Gabriel Sainte-Marie, have claimed that privatization would be done at the expense of residential customers, who would pay much higher rates. They say that privatization would also be a betrayal of the social pact between the people and its government, and that the province would be short-selling itself by divesting of a choice asset for a minimal short term gain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Activities">Activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Power_generation">Power generation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Power generation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_power_stations_in_Quebec" title="List of power stations in Quebec">List of power stations in Quebec</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Barrage_Daniel-Johnson2.jpg"><img alt="A large concrete dam with multiple arches" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Barrage_Daniel-Johnson2.jpg/440px-Barrage_Daniel-Johnson2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Barrage_Daniel-Johnson2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe Daniel-Johnson Dam on the <a href="/wiki/Manicouagan_River" title="Manicouagan River">Manicouagan River</a>, supplying the Manic-5 hydro plant.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright" style="">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px">\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue"></div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<p>Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec sources of energy supply (2013)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2013HQSupplies_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-2013HQSupplies-52">[51]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0Hydro (96.8%)</div>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:MediumSeaGreen; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0Other Renewables (2.9%)</div>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Crimson; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0Nuclear (0.2%)</div>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Gray; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0Thermal (0.1%)</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>On December 31, 2013, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec Production owned and operated 61 <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">hydro</a> plants\xe2\x80\x94including 12 of over a 1,000 MW capacity\xe2\x80\x94 26 major reservoirs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2011a8_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2011a8-53">[52]</a></sup> These facilities are located in 13 of Quebec\'s 430 <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">watersheds</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGovernment_of_Quebec2002.3F_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGovernment_of_Quebec2002.3F-54">[53]</a></sup> including the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_River" title="Saint Lawrence River">Saint Lawrence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Betsiamites_River" title="Betsiamites River">Betsiamites</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Grande_River" title="La Grande River">La Grande</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manicouagan_River" title="Manicouagan River">Manicouagan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottawa_River" title="Ottawa River">Ottawa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rivi%C3%A8re_aux_Outardes" title="Rivi\xc3\xa8re aux Outardes">Outardes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saint-Maurice_River" title="Saint-Maurice River">Saint-Maurice</a> rivers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup> These plants provide the bulk of electricity generated and sold by the company.</p>\n<p>Non-hydro plants included the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Base_load_power_plant" title="Base load power plant">baseload</a> 675-MW gross <a href="/wiki/Gentilly_Nuclear_Generating_Station" title="Gentilly Nuclear Generating Station">Gentilly nuclear generating station</a>, a <a href="/wiki/CANDU_reactor" title="CANDU reactor">CANDU-design reactor</a> which was permanently shut down on December 28, 2012<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gentilly_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gentilly-56">[55]</a></sup> the 660-MW <a href="/wiki/Tracy_Thermal_Generating_Station" title="Tracy Thermal Generating Station">Tracy Thermal Generating Station</a>, a heavy fuel oil-fired plant shutdown in March 2011<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> and two <a href="/wiki/Gas_turbine" title="Gas turbine">gas turbine</a> <a href="/wiki/Peaking_power_plant" title="Peaking power plant">peaker plants</a>, for a total installed capacity of 36,971 MW in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012a114_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012a114-58">[57]</a></sup> Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec\'s average generation cost was 2.11 cents per kWh in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2011a12_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2011a12-59">[58]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The company also purchases the bulk of the output of the 5,428-MW Churchill Falls generating station in Labrador, under a long term contract expiring in 2041.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2011a92_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2011a92-60">[59]</a></sup> In 2009, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec bought the 60% stake owned by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AbitibiBowater" title="AbitibiBowater">AbitibiBowater</a> in the <a href="/wiki/McCormick_Dam" title="McCormick Dam">McCormick plant</a> (335 MW), located at the mouth of the Manicouagan River near <a href="/wiki/Baie-Comeau" title="Baie-Comeau">Baie-Comeau</a>, for C$616 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2010a10_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2010a10-61">[60]</a></sup></p>\n<table class="wikitable center" style="text-align:left; width:60%;">\n<caption><b>Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec Production main power
