title="Jean-Lesage generating station">Jean-Lesage</a></td>\n<td>Manicouagan</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">1,145</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Daniel-Johnson_Dam" title="Daniel-Johnson Dam">Manic-5-PA</a></td>\n<td>Manicouagan</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">1,064</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Outardes-3" title="Outardes-3">Outardes-3</a></td>\n<td>aux Outardes</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">1,026</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2">Others (47 hydro, 1 nuclear, 3 thermal)</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">13,302</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>In 2013, the energy sold by Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec to its grid-connected customers in Quebec and exported to neighboring markets came almost exclusively from renewable sources. Hydro (96.78%) is by far the largest source, followed by wind (2.16%) and biomass, biogas and waste (0.75%). The remainder came from nuclear (0.19%) and thermal (0.12%) generation. Emissions of carbon dioxide (1,130 tonnes/TWh), <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">sulfur dioxide</a> (4 tonnes/TWh) and <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_oxide" title="Nitrogen oxide">nitrogen oxides</a> (10 tonnes/TWh) were between 49 and 238 times lower than the industry average in northeastern North America. Imported electricity bought on the markets account for most of these emissions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2013HQSupplies_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-2013HQSupplies-52">[51]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transmission_system">Transmission system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Transmission system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec%27s_electricity_transmission_system" title="Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec\'s electricity transmission system">Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec\'s electricity transmission system</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Poste_Micoua.jpg"><img alt="Power lines reach a hub in a densely forested area. A road going downhill leads to a forest of metal pylons." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Poste_Micoua.jpg/220px-Poste_Micoua.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Poste_Micoua.jpg/330px-Poste_Micoua.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Poste_Micoua.jpg/440px-Poste_Micoua.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Poste_Micoua.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe Micoua substation on the North Shore of Quebec. This facility converts 315 kV power coming from five hydro plant to 735 kV. This Trans\xc3\x89nergie facility is one of the main nodes of the 11,422-kilometre (7,097\xc2\xa0mi) long 735 kV network.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec\'s expertise at building and operating a very high voltage electrical grid spreading over long distances has long been recognized in the electrical industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHafsi2001561.E2.80.93562_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHafsi2001561.E2.80.93562-63">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Farley_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Farley-64">[62]</a></sup> Trans\xc3\x89nergie, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec\'s transmission division, operates the largest electricity transmission network in North America. It acts as the independent system operator and reliability coordinator for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qu%C3%A9bec_Interconnection" title="Qu\xc3\xa9bec Interconnection">Qu\xc3\xa9bec interconnection</a> of the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Electric_Reliability_Corporation" title="North American Electric Reliability Corporation">North American Electric Reliability Corporation</a> system, and is part of the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Power_Coordinating_Council" title="Northeast Power Coordinating Council">Northeast Power Coordinating Council</a> (NPCC). Trans\xc3\x89nergie manages the flow of energy on the Quebec network and ensures non-discriminatory access to all participants involved in the wholesale market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HQT_profil_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-HQT_profil-65">[63]</a></sup> The non-discriminatory access policy allows a company such as <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador_Hydro" title="Newfoundland and Labrador Hydro">Nalcor</a> to sell some of its share of power from Churchill Falls on the open market in the State of New York using Trans\xc3\x89nergie\'s network, upon payment of a transmission fee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In recent years, Trans\xc3\x89nergie\'s <i>Contr\xc3\xb4le des mouvements d\'\xc3\xa9nergie</i> (CM\xc3\x89) unit has been acting as the reliability coordinator of the bulk electricity network for Quebec as a whole, under a bilateral agreement between the R\xc3\xa9gie de l\'\xc3\xa9nergie du Qu\xc3\xa9bec and the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Energy_Regulatory_Commission" title="Federal Energy Regulatory Commission">Federal Energy Regulatory Commission</a> of the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Trans\xc3\x89nergie\'s high voltage network stretches over 33,630\xc2\xa0km (20,900\xc2\xa0mi), including 11,422\xc2\xa0km (7,097\xc2\xa0mi) of <span class="nowrap">765 and 735 kV lines</span>, and a network of 514 substations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012a14_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012a14-69">[67]</a></sup> It is connected to neighbouring Canadian provinces and the United States by 17 ties, with a maximum reception capacity of 10,850 MW<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[note 3]</a></sup> and a maximum transmission capacity of 7,994 MW.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[68]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Interconnections">Interconnections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Interconnections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HQ_-_Poste_Outaouais_1.jpg"><img alt="A yellow-tinted room with wires and other metallic structures." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/HQ_-_Poste_Outaouais_1.jpg/170px-HQ_-_Poste_Outaouais_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/HQ_-_Poste_Outaouais_1.jpg/255px-HQ_-_Poste_Outaouais_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/HQ_-_Poste_Outaouais_1.jpg/340px-HQ_-_Poste_Outaouais_1.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HQ_-_Poste_Outaouais_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA rectifier at the Outaouais substation, located in <a href="/wiki/L%27Ange-Gardien,_Outaouais,_Quebec" title="L\'Ange-Gardien, Outaouais, Quebec">L\'Ange-Gardien</a>. The 1,250 MW back-to-back <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HVDC" title="HVDC">HVDC</a> tie links the Quebec grid with Ontario\'s <a href="/wiki/Hydro_One" title="Hydro One">Hydro One</a> network.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The Trans\xc3\x89nergie\'s network operates asynchronously from that of its neighbours on the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Interconnection" title="Eastern Interconnection">Eastern Interconnection</a>. Although Quebec uses the same 60 <a href="/wiki/Hertz" title="Hertz">hertz</a> frequency as the rest of North America, its grid does not use the same phase as surrounding networks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HQ_Outaouais_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-HQ_Outaouais-72">[69]</a></sup> Trans\xc3\x89nergie mainly relies on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HVDC#Back_to_back" title="HVDC">back to back HVDC</a> converters to export or import electricity from other jurisdictions.</p>\n<p>This feature of the Quebec network allowed Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec to remain unscathed during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northeast_Blackout_of_2003" title="Northeast Blackout of 2003">Northeast Blackout of August 14, 2003</a>, with the exception of 5 hydro plants on the <a href="/wiki/Ottawa_River" title="Ottawa River">Ottawa River</a> radially connected to the Ontario grid at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[70]</a></sup> A new 1250-MW back to back HVDC tie has been commissioned at the Outaouais substation, in <a href="/wiki/L%27Ange-Gardien,_Outaouais,_Quebec" title="L\'Ange-Gardien, Outaouais, Quebec">L\'Ange-Gardien</a>, near the <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a> border. The new interconnection has been online since 2009 and the 315 kV line is fully operational since 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HQ_Outaouais_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-HQ_Outaouais-72">[69]</a></sup></p>\n<p>One drawback of the Trans\xc3\x89nergie network involves the long distances separating the generation sites and the main consumer markets. For instance, the <a href="/wiki/Radisson,_Quebec" title="Radisson, Quebec">Radisson</a> substation links the James Bay project plants to the Nicolet station near <a href="/wiki/Sainte-Eulalie,_Quebec" title="Sainte-Eulalie, Quebec">Sainte-Eulalie</a>, south of the Saint Lawrence, over 1,200 kilometres (750\xc2\xa0mi) away.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[71]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Investments">Investments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Investments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In 2011, Trans\xc3\x89nergie invested C$1.3 billion in capital expenditures, including C$460 million to expand its network.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012a15_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012a15-75">[72]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In addition to the new tie with Ontario, the company plans to build a new 1200-MW direct current link between the Des Cantons substation at <a href="/wiki/Windsor,_Quebec" title="Windsor, Quebec">Windsor, Quebec</a> in Quebec\'s <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Townships" title="Eastern Townships">Eastern Townships</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deerfield,_New_Hampshire" title="Deerfield, New Hampshire">Deerfield, New Hampshire</a>, with an HVDC converter terminal built at <a href="/wiki/Franklin,_New_Hampshire" title="Franklin, New Hampshire">Franklin, New Hampshire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[73]</a></sup> The US segment of the US$1.1 billion line,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[74]</a></sup> would be built by <i>Northern Pass Transmission LLC</i>, a partnership between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northeast_Utilities" title="Northeast Utilities">Northeast Utilities</a> (75%) and <a href="/wiki/NSTAR_(company)" title="NSTAR (company)">NSTAR</a> (25%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[75]</a></sup> In order to go ahead, the project must receive regulatory approval in Quebec and the United States. The proposed transmission line could be in operation in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[76]</a></sup> According to Jim Robb, a senior executive from Northeast Utilities, <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> could meet one third of its <a href="/wiki/Regional_Greenhouse_Gas_Initiative" title="Regional Greenhouse Gas Initiative">Regional Greenhouse Gas Initiative</a> commitments with the hydropower coming through this new power line alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[77]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Distribution">Distribution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Distribution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec_transformateur.jpg"><img alt="A man with a hard hat helps a machinery operator lower a transformer to an underground pit in a residential neighborhood. The roads and cars are covered with snow." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1800" data-file-width="2700" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec_transformateur.jpg/220px-Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec_transformateur.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec_transformateur.jpg/330px-Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec_transformateur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec_transformateur.jpg/440px-Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec_transformateur.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec_transformateur.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nAn Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec employee carries out the replacement of an underground transformer in Montreal.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec Distribution is in charge of retail sales to most customers in Quebec. It operates a network of 112,089 kilometres (69,649\xc2\xa0mi) of medium and <a href="/wiki/Low_voltage" title="Low voltage">low voltage</a> lines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2011a20_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2011a20-81">[78]</a></sup> The division is the sole electric distributor across the province, with the exception of 9 municipal distribution networks \xe2\x80\x94 in <a href="/wiki/Alma,_Quebec" title="Alma, Quebec">Alma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amos,_Quebec" title="Amos, Quebec">Amos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baie-Comeau" title="Baie-Comeau">Baie-Comeau</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coaticook,_Quebec" title="Coaticook, Quebec">Coaticook</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joliette" title="Joliette">Joliette</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magog,_Quebec" title="Magog, Quebec">Magog</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saguenay,_Quebec" title="Saguenay, Quebec">Saguenay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sherbrooke" title="Sherbrooke">Sherbrooke</a> and <a href="/wiki/Westmount,_Quebec" title="Westmount, Quebec">Westmount</a>\xe2\x80\x94and the electric cooperative of <a href="/wiki/Saint-Jean-Baptiste,_Quebec" title="Saint-Jean-Baptiste, Quebec">Saint-Jean-Baptiste de Rouville</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[79]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec Distribution buys most of its power from the 165-TWh <i>heritage pool</i> provided by Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec Production at 2.79\xc2\xa2/<a href="/wiki/Kilowatt_hour" title="Kilowatt hour">kWh</a>. The division usually purchases additional power by entering into long-term contracts after a public call for tenders. For shorter term needs, it also buys power from the neighboring systems at market prices. As a last resort, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec Production can also provide short-term relief.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HQ2007_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-HQ2007-31">[31]</a></sup> Supply contracts above and beyond the heritage pool must be approved by the <i>R\xc3\xa9gie de l\'\xc3\xa9nergie du Qu\xc3\xa9bec</i> and their costs are passed on to customers.</p>\n<p>The division signed one <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> <a href="/wiki/Cogeneration" title="Cogeneration">cogeneration</a> agreement for 507 MW in 2003, three forest biomass deals (47.5 MW) in 2004 and 2005, and ten contracts for <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind power</a> (2,994 MW) in 2005 and 2008, all with private sector producers. It also signed two flexible contracts with Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec Production (600 MW) in 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[80]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec Distribution is also responsible for the production of power in remote communities not connected to the main power grid. The division operates an off-grid hydroelectric dam serving communities on the <a href="/wiki/Basse-C%C3%B4te-Nord" title="Basse-C\xc3\xb4te-Nord">Lower North Shore</a> and 23 small diesel power plants in the <a href="/wiki/Magdalen_Islands" title="Magdalen Islands">Magdalen Islands</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Mauricie" title="Mauricie">Haute-Mauricie</a> and in <a href="/wiki/Nunavik" title="Nunavik">Nunavik</a>.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_activities">Other activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Other activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_and_development">Research and development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Research and development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Institut_de_recherche_d%27Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Institut de recherche d\'Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec">Institut de recherche d\'Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TM4_Electrodynamic_Systems" title="TM4 Electrodynamic Systems">TM4 Electrodynamic Systems</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tata_Indica_EV_Engine_bay.jpg"><img alt="A demonstration car with an electric engine is shown as an exhibit." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Tata_Indica_EV_Engine_bay.jpg/220px-Tata_Indica_EV_Engine_bay.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Tata_Indica_EV_Engine_bay.jpg/330px-Tata_Indica_EV_Engine_bay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Tata_Indica_EV_Engine_bay.jpg/440px-Tata_Indica_EV_Engine_bay.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tata_Indica_EV_Engine_bay.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe TM4 electric engine was developed by Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mitsubishi_i-MiEV_Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec.JPG"><img alt="A small curved car at an automobile show." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="639" data-file-width="985" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Mitsubishi_i-MiEV_Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec.JPG/220px-Mitsubishi_i-MiEV_Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Mitsubishi_i-MiEV_Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec.JPG/330px-Mitsubishi_i-MiEV_Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Mitsubishi_i-MiEV_Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec.JPG/440px-Mitsubishi_i-MiEV_Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mitsubishi_i-MiEV_Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA Hydro-Quebec <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_i_MiEV" title="Mitsubishi i MiEV">Mitsubishi i MiEV</a> vehicle from the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Montreal_International_Auto_Show" title="Montreal International Auto Show">Montreal International Auto Show</a>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec has made significant investments in research and development over the past 40 years. In addition to funding university research, the company is the only electric utility in North America to operate its own large-scale research institute, L\'<a href="/wiki/Institut_de_recherche_d%27Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Institut de recherche d\'Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec">Institut de recherche d\'Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec</a> (IREQ). Established by <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Boulet" title="Lionel Boulet">Lionel Boulet</a> in 1967, the research centre is located in <a href="/wiki/Varennes,_Quebec" title="Varennes, Quebec">Varennes</a>, a suburb on the <a href="/wiki/South_Shore_(Montreal)" title="South Shore (Montreal)">South Shore</a> of <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IREQ_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-IREQ-84">[81]</a></sup> IREQ operates on an annual research budget of approximately C$100 million<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2011a32_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2011a32-85">[82]</a></sup> and specializes in the areas of high voltage, <a href="/wiki/Mechanics" title="Mechanics">mechanics</a> and thermomechanics, network simulations and calibration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[83]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Research conducted by scientists and engineers at IREQ has helped to extend the life of dams, improve <a href="/wiki/Water_turbine" title="Water turbine">water turbine</a> performance, automate network management and increase the transmission capacity of high voltage power lines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[84]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Another research centre, the <i>Laboratoire des technologies de l\'\xc3\xa9nergie</i> (LTE) in Shawinigan, was opened in 1988<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forces_IREQ_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Forces_IREQ-88">[85]</a></sup> to adapt and develop new products while helping industrial customers improve their energy efficiency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[86]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In the last 20 years, the institute has also conducted <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a> work towards the <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle" title="Electric vehicle">electrification of ground transportation</a>. Current projects include <a href="/wiki/Battery_(electricity)" title="Battery (electricity)">battery</a> materials, including innovative work on <a href="/wiki/Lithium_iron_phosphate" title="Lithium iron phosphate">lithium iron phosphate</a> and nano-titanate,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[87]</a></sup> improved electric <a href="/wiki/Powertrain" title="Powertrain">drive trains</a> and the effects of the large-scale deployment of electric vehicles on the <a href="/wiki/Electrical_grid" title="Electrical grid">power grid</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2011a36.E2.80.9337_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2011a36.E2.80.9337-91">[88]</a></sup> Projects focus on technologies to increase <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Range_(vehicle)" title="Range (vehicle)">range</a>, improve performance in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cold_weather" title="Cold weather">cold weather</a> and reduce <a href="/wiki/Rechargeable_battery" title="Rechargeable battery">charging time</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[89]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec has been criticized for not having taken advantage of some of its innovations. An electric <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wheel_motor" title="Wheel motor">wheel motor</a> concept that struck a chord with Quebecers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[90]</a></sup> first prototyped in 1994 by Pierre Couture, an engineer and <a href="/wiki/Physicist" title="Physicist">physicist</a> working at IREQ, is one of these.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[92]</a></sup> The heir to the Couture wheel motor is now marketed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TM4_Electrodynamic_Systems" title="TM4 Electrodynamic Systems">TM4 Electrodynamic Systems</a>, a spin-off established in 1998<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[93]</a></sup> that has made deals with France\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dassault" title="Dassault">Dassault</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heuliez" title="Heuliez">Heuliez</a> to develop an electric car, the <a href="/wiki/Cleanova" title="Cleanova">Cleanova</a>, of which prototypes were built in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[94]</a></sup> Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec announced in early 2009 at the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_International_Auto_Show" title="Montreal International Auto Show">Montreal International Auto Show</a> that its engine had been chosen by <a href="/wiki/Tata_Motors" title="Tata Motors">Tata Motors</a> to equip a demonstration version of its <a href="/wiki/Tata_Indica" title="Tata Indica">Indica</a> model, which will be road tested in <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[96]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction">Construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec \xc3\x89quipement division acts as the company\'s main contractor on major construction sites, with the exception of work conducted on the territory covered by the <a href="/wiki/James_Bay_and_Northern_Quebec_Agreement" title="James Bay and Northern Quebec Agreement">James Bay and Northern Quebec Agreement</a>, which are assigned to the <a href="/wiki/James_Bay_Energy" title="James Bay Energy">Soci\xc3\xa9t\xc3\xa9 d\'\xc3\xa9nergie de la Baie James</a> subsidiary.</p>\n<p>The construction of a complex of four hydroelectric generating stations on the Romaine River (<span class="nowrap">1,550 MW</span>) began on May 13, 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[97]</a></sup> The plants are scheduled to be built and commissioned between 2014 and 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[98]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In his March 2009 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Throne_speech" title="Throne speech">inaugural speech</a>, Quebec Premier <a href="/wiki/Jean_Charest" title="Jean Charest">Jean Charest</a> announced that his government intends to further develop the province\'s hydroelectric potential.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[99]</a></sup> The call for further development of hydroelectric and other renewable generating capacity has been implemented in the company\'s 2009-2013 strategic plan, released on July 30, 2009. Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec plans capacity upgrades at the <a href="/wiki/Jean-Lesage_generating_station" title="Jean-Lesage generating station">Jean-Lesage</a> (120 MW) and <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9-L%C3%A9vesque_generating_station" title="Ren\xc3\xa9-L\xc3\xa9vesque generating station">Ren\xc3\xa9-L\xc3\xa9vesque</a> (210 MW) stations and a third unit at the SM-3 plant (440 MW). The company will also conduct technical and environmental studies and undertake consultations with local communities to build new facilities on the Petit-M\xc3\xa9catina (1,200 MW) and Magpie (850 MW) rivers on the North Shore, and revive the Tabaret project (132 MW) in the <a href="/wiki/Abitibi-T%C3%A9miscamingue" title="Abitibi-T\xc3\xa9miscamingue">Abitibi-T\xc3\xa9miscamingue</a> region, in western Quebec.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2009a19_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2009a19-103">[100]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="International_ventures">International ventures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: International ventures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec first forays outside its borders began in 1978. A new subsidiary, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec International, was created to market the company\'s know-how abroad in the fields of distribution, generation and transmission of electricity. The new venture leveraged the existing pool of expertise in the parent company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECloutier1984172.E2.80.93174_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECloutier1984172.E2.80.93174-104">[101]</a></sup></p>\n<p>During the next 25 years, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec was particularly active abroad with investments in electricity transmission networks and generation: Transelec in <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[102]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Cross_Sound_Cable" title="Cross Sound Cable">Cross Sound Cable</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Farley_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-Farley-64">[62]</a></sup> the Consorcio Transmantaro in <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>, Hidroelectrica Rio Lajas in <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Murraylink" title="Murraylink">Murraylink</a> in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Fortuna_Dam" title="Fortuna Dam">Fortuna generating station</a> in <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[103]</a></sup></p>\n<p>It briefly held a 17% share in SENELEC, <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a>\'s electric utility, when the Senegalese government decided to sell part of the company to a consortium led by the French company Elyo, a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Suez_(company)" title="Suez (company)">Group Suez Lyonnaise des Eaux</a>, in 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HQ1999_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-HQ1999-107">[104]</a></sup> The transaction was canceled in 2000 following the election of president <a href="/wiki/Abdoulaye_Wade" title="Abdoulaye Wade">Abdoulaye Wade</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[105]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Also in 1999, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec International acquired a 20% stake in the Meiya Power Company in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People\'s Republic of China">China</a> for C$83 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HQ1999_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-HQ1999-107">[104]</a></sup> The company held this participation until July 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[106]</a></sup> The company\'s expertise was sought by several hydroelectric developers throughout the world, including the <a href="/wiki/Three_Gorges_Dam" title="Three Gorges Dam">Three Gorges Dam</a>, where Hydro\'s employees trained Chinese engineers in the fields of management, finance and dams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[107]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec gradually withdrew from the international business between 2003 and 2006, and sold off all of its foreign investments for a profit. Proceeds from these sales were paid to the government\'s Generations Fund, a trust fund set up by the province to alleviate the effect of public debt on future generations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[108]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brochet_Luc_Viatour.jpg"><img alt="A fish." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2440" data-file-width="3572" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Brochet_Luc_Viatour.jpg/220px-Brochet_Luc_Viatour.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Brochet_Luc_Viatour.jpg/330px-Brochet_Luc_Viatour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Brochet_Luc_Viatour.jpg/440px-Brochet_Luc_Viatour.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brochet_Luc_Viatour.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Northern_pike" title="Northern pike">northern pike</a> (<i>Esox lucius</i>) is more prevalent today in the <a href="/wiki/Robert-Bourassa_Reservoir" title="Robert-Bourassa Reservoir">Robert-Bourassa Reservoir</a> than it was before the flooding of the reservoir. The increase of this population has been counterbalanced by a decline in the <a href="/wiki/Walleye" title="Walleye">walleye</a> (Stizostedion vitreum) population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[109]</a></sup></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The construction and operation of electric generation, transmission and distribution facilities has environmental effects and Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec\'s activities are no exception. Hydroelectric development affects the natural environment where facilities are built and on the people living in the area. For instance, the development of new reservoirs increases the level of mercury in lakes and rivers, which works up the food chain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HQ_Hg_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-HQ_Hg-113">[110]</a></sup> It temporarily increases the emission of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gases" title="Greenhouse gases">greenhouse gases</a> from reservoirs<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HQ_GES_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-HQ_GES-114">[111]</a></sup> and contributes to shoreline erosion.</p>\n<p>In addition, hydroelectric facilities transform the human environment. They create new obstacles to navigation, flood traditional hunting and trapping grounds, force people to change their eating habits due to the elevated mercury content of some species of fish, destroy invaluable artifacts that would help trace the human presence on the territory, and disrupt the society and culture of Aboriginal people living near the facilities.</p>\n<p>Since the early 1970s, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec has been aware of the environmental externalities of its operations. The adoption of a Quebec statute on environmental quality in 1972, the cancellation of Champigny Project, a planned <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pumped_storage" title="Pumped storage">pumped storage</a> plant in the <a href="/wiki/Jacques-Cartier_River" title="Jacques-Cartier River">Jacques-Cartier River</a> valley in 1973, and the James Bay negotiations leading to the <a href="/wiki/James_Bay_and_Northern_Quebec_Agreement" title="James Bay and Northern Quebec Agreement">James Bay and Northern Quebec Agreement</a> in 1975, forced the company to reconsider its practices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDubeau1995242_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDubeau1995242-115">[112]</a></sup></p>\n<p>To address environmental concerns, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec established an environmental protection committee in 1970 and an Environmental Management unit in September 1973.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDubeau1995241_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDubeau1995241-116">[113]</a></sup> Its mandate is to study and measure the environmental effects of the company, prepare impact assessment, and develop mitigation strategies for new and existing facilities, while conducting research projects in these areas, in cooperation with the scientific community.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects_on_the_natural_environment">Effects on the natural environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Effects on the natural environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Caribou_traversant_la_rivi%C3%A8re_aux_Feuilles.jpg"><img alt="A herd of Cariboo crossing a remote river." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Caribou_traversant_la_rivi%C3%A8re_aux_Feuilles.jpg/220px-Caribou_traversant_la_rivi%C3%A8re_aux_Feuilles.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Caribou_traversant_la_rivi%C3%A8re_aux_Feuilles.jpg/330px-Caribou_traversant_la_rivi%C3%A8re_aux_Feuilles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Caribou_traversant_la_rivi%C3%A8re_aux_Feuilles.jpg/440px-Caribou_traversant_la_rivi%C3%A8re_aux_Feuilles.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Caribou_traversant_la_rivi%C3%A8re_aux_Feuilles.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caribou" title="Caribou">caribou</a> population near major reservoirs in northern Quebec has increased between 1970 and 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHayeur2001110_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayeur2001110-117">[114]</a></sup></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>In the late 1970s, the company set up a network of 27 monitoring stations to measure the effects of the James Bay Project<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDubeau1995243_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDubeau1995243-118">[115]</a></sup> which provide a wealth of data on northern environments. The first 30 years of studies in the James Bay area have confirmed that mercury levels in fish increase by 3 to 6 times over the first 5 to 10 years after the flooding of a reservoir, but then gradually revert to their initial values after 20 to 30 years. These results confirm similar studies conducted elsewhere in Canada, the United States and Finland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHayeur2001110_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayeur2001110-117">[114]</a></sup> Research also found that it is possible to reduce human exposure to mercury even when fish constitutes a significant part of a population\'s diet. Exposure risks can be mitigated without overly reducing the consumption of fish, simply by avoiding certain species and fishing spots.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHayeur2001110_117-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayeur2001110-117">[114]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Despite the fact that the transformation of a terrestrial environment into an aquatic environment constitutes a major change and that flooding leads to the displacement or death of nonmigratory animals, the riparian environments lost through flooding are partially replaced by new ones on the exposed banks of reduced-flow rivers. The biological diversity of reservoir islands is comparable to other islands in the area and the reservoir <a href="/wiki/Drawdown_(hydrology)" title="Drawdown (hydrology)">drawdown</a> zone is used by a variety of wildlife. The population of migratory species of interest such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caribou" title="Caribou">caribou</a> have even increased to the point where the hunt has been expanded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHayeur200189_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayeur200189-119">[116]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Emissions of greenhouse gases (GHG) rise significantly for a few years after reservoir impoundment, and then stabilize after 10 years to a level similar to that of surrounding lakes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HQ_GES_114-1"><a href="#cite_note-HQ_GES-114">[111]</a></sup> Gross GHG emissions of reservoirs in the James Bay area fluctuate around 30,000 tonnes of CO<sub>2</sub> equivalent per TWh of generated power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[117]</a></sup> Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec claims its hydroelectric plants release 35 times less GHG than comparable gas-fired plants and 70 times less than coal-fired ones and that they constitute the "option with the best performance" overall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HQ_GES_114-2"><a href="#cite_note-HQ_GES-114">[111]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_effects_and_sustainable_development">Social effects and sustainable development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Social effects and sustainable development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:03_Chisasibi_-_welcome_sign_closeup.jpg"><img alt="A road sign welcoming people to Chisasibi." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1200" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/03_Chisasibi_-_welcome_sign_closeup.jpg/220px-03_Chisasibi_-_welcome_sign_closeup.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/03_Chisasibi_-_welcome_sign_closeup.jpg/330px-03_Chisasibi_-_welcome_sign_closeup.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/03_Chisasibi_-_welcome_sign_closeup.jpg/440px-03_Chisasibi_-_welcome_sign_closeup.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:03_Chisasibi_-_welcome_sign_closeup.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nOf all Cree communities, <a href="/wiki/Chisasibi" title="Chisasibi">Chisasibi</a> was most affected by the James Bay hydroelectric development project<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHayeur2001110_117-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayeur2001110-117">[114]</a></sup> Crees living on Fort George island resettled to the new village on the left bank of La Grande River in 1980-1981.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Another major environmental concern relates to the population of areas affected by hydroelectric development, specifically the <a href="/wiki/Innu" title="Innu">Innu</a> of the North Shore and the <a href="/wiki/Cree" title="Cree">Cree</a> and <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a> in Northern Quebec. The hydroelectric developments of the last quarter of the 20th century have accelerated the settling process among Aboriginal populations that started in the 1950s. Among the reasons cited for the increased adoption of a sedentary lifestyle among these peoples are the establishment of Aboriginal businesses, the introduction of paid labor, and the flooding of traditional trapping and fishing lands by the new reservoirs, along with the operation of social and education services run by the communities themselves under the <a href="/wiki/James_Bay_and_Northern_Quebec_Agreement" title="James Bay and Northern Quebec Agreement">James Bay and Northern Quebec Agreement</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHayeur200189_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayeur200189-119">[116]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Some native communities, particularly the Crees, have come to a point "where they increasingly resemble the industrialized society of the South", notes an Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec report summarizing the research conducted in the area between 1970 and 2000. The report adds that a similar phenomenon was observed after the construction of roads and hydroelectric plants near isolated communities in northern Canada and Scandinavia. However, growing social problems and rising unemployment have followed the end of the large construction projects in the 1990s. The report concludes that future economic and social development in the area "will largely depend on the desire for cooperation among the various players".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHayeur200189_119-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHayeur200189-119">[116]</a></sup></p>\n<p>After the strong rejection of the Suro\xc3\xaet project and its subsequent cancellation in November 2004, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec, under the leadership of its new CEO <a href="/wiki/Thierry_Vandal" title="Thierry Vandal">Thierry Vandal</a>, reaffirmed Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec\'s commitment towards energy efficiency, hydropower and development of alternative energy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVandal2005236_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVandal2005236-121">[118]</a></sup> Since then, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec regularly stresses three criteria for any new hydroelectric development undertaken by the company: projects must be cost effective, environmentally acceptable and well received by the communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HQ2007_31-2"><a href="#cite_note-HQ2007-31">[31]</a></sup> Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec has also taken part in a series of <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_development" title="Sustainable development">sustainable development</a> initiatives since the late 1980s. Its approach is based on three principles: economic development, social development and environmental protection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[119]</a></sup> Since 2007 the company adheres to the <a href="/wiki/Global_Reporting_Initiative" title="Global Reporting Initiative">Global Reporting Initiative</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[120]</a></sup> which governs the collection and publication of sustainability performance information. The company employs 250 professionals and managers in the environmental field and has implemented an <a href="/wiki/ISO_14000" title="ISO 14000">ISO 14001</a>-certified environmental management system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[121]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rates_and_customers">Rates and customers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Rates and customers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Quebec_market">Quebec market</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Quebec market">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable centre" style="text-align:right; width:95%;">\n<caption><b>Operating statistics as of December 31, 2010 and 2011</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012a96_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012a96-125">[122]</a></sup></caption>\n<tr>\n<th rowspan="2" scope="col" style="width:28%; background:#ddd;">10,720</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">10,506</td>\n<td style="text-align:right; background:#ddd;"></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;"></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hq_tarifs-ipc-en.svg"><img alt="Graph showing the evolution of inflation and Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec rates. Inflation raised more rapidly than Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec\'s residential rate between 1998 and 2011." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="528" data-file-width="819" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Hq_tarifs-ipc-en.svg/220px-Hq_tarifs-ipc-en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Hq_tarifs-ipc-en.svg/330px-Hq_tarifs-ipc-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Hq_tarifs-ipc-en.svg/440px-Hq_tarifs-ipc-en.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hq_tarifs-ipc-en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nEvolution of Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec residential rates (turquoise) and the Quebec <a href="/wiki/Consumer_price_index" title="Consumer price index">Consumer price index</a> (dark blue) between 1998 and 2011.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>At the end of 2010, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec served 4,060,195 customers<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012a96_125-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012a96-125">[122]</a></sup> grouped into three broad categories: residential and farm (D Rate), commercial and institutional (G Rate) and industrial (M and L rates). The <i>Other</i> category includes public lighting systems and municipal distribution systems.</p>\n<p>About a dozen distribution rates are set annually by the <i>R\xc3\xa9gie de l\'\xc3\xa9nergie</i> after public hearings. Pricing is based on the cost of delivery, which includes the cost of supply and transmission, depreciation on fixed assets and provisions for the maintenance of facilities, customer growth and a profit margin.</p>\n<p>Rates are uniform throughout Quebec and are based on consumer type and volume of consumption. All rates vary in block to mitigate any cross-subsidization effect between residential, commercial and industrial customers.</p>\n<p>Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec retail rates are among the lowest in North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[123]</a></sup> After a five-year rate freeze, between May 1, 1998 and January 1, 2004,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[124]</a></sup> the <i>R\xc3\xa9gie</i> granted rate increases on 8 occasions between 2004 and 2010 for a total of 18.4%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[125]</a></sup> More recently, the regulator ordered two successive rate rollbacks in 2011 (0.4%) and 2012 (0.5%). However, rates are expected to go up by 3.7% a year from 2014 to 2018 to reflect a gradual increase of heritage pool electricity announced in the 2010 Quebec budget.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[126]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Residential_customers">Residential customers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Residential customers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thermostat_%C3%A9lectronique.jpg"><img alt="Electronic thermostat showing a temperature of 22\xc2\xb0C." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2004" data-file-width="2080" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Thermostat_%C3%A9lectronique.jpg/140px-Thermostat_%C3%A9lectronique.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Thermostat_%C3%A9lectronique.jpg/210px-Thermostat_%C3%A9lectronique.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Thermostat_%C3%A9lectronique.jpg/280px-Thermostat_%C3%A9lectronique.jpg 2x" width="140"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Thermostat_%C3%A9lectronique.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nElectric heating accounts for more than half of the electricity used by residential customers in Quebec, according to Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The average consumption of residential and agricultural customers is relatively high, at 16,857 kWh per year in 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012a96_125-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012a96-125">[122]</a></sup> because of the widespread use of electricity as the main source of <a href="/wiki/Electric_heating" title="Electric heating">space</a> (77%) and <a href="/wiki/Water_heating" title="Water heating">water heating</a> (90%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012b14_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012b14-130">[127]</a></sup> Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec estimates that heating accounts for more than one half of the electricity demand in the residential sector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[128]</a></sup></p>\n<p>This preference for electric heating makes electricity demand more unpredictable, but offers some environmental benefits. Despite Quebec\'s very cold climate in winter, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gases" title="Greenhouse gases">greenhouse gases</a> emissions in the residential sector accounted for only 5.5% (4.65 Mt <span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><br/>\n2</span></span> eq.) of all emissions in Quebec in 2006. Emissions from the residential sector in Quebec fell by 30% between 1990 and 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[129]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Residential use of electricity fluctuates from one year to another, and is strongly <a href="/wiki/Correlation_and_dependence" title="Correlation and dependence">correlated</a> with the weather. Contrary to the trend in neighboring networks, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec\'s system is winter-<a href="/wiki/Peak_demand" title="Peak demand">peaking</a>. A new all-time consumption record was set on January 23, 2013 with a load of <span class="nowrap">38,910 MW</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[130]</a></sup> Previous records were established on January 24, 2011 with <span class="nowrap">37,717 MW</span>, on January 16, 2009, with a load of <span class="nowrap">37,230 MW</span>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2010a20_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2010a20-134">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[132]</a></sup> and on January 15, 2004 when peak reached <span class="nowrap">36,268 MW</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[133]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:92px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Landis%2BGyr_FocusAXR-SD_Hydro-Quebec.JPG"><img alt="A 2010s-style digital power meter." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1820" data-file-width="1820" height="90" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Landis%2BGyr_FocusAXR-SD_Hydro-Quebec.JPG/90px-Landis%2BGyr_FocusAXR-SD_Hydro-Quebec.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Landis%2BGyr_FocusAXR-SD_Hydro-Quebec.JPG/135px-Landis%2BGyr_FocusAXR-SD_Hydro-Quebec.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Landis%2BGyr_FocusAXR-SD_Hydro-Quebec.JPG/180px-Landis%2BGyr_FocusAXR-SD_Hydro-Quebec.JPG 2x" width="90"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Landis%2BGyr_FocusAXR-SD_Hydro-Quebec.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec digital power meter.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The price of electricity for residences and farms includes a 40.64\xc2\xa2 daily subscription fee, and two price levels depending on consumption. The rates are all-included: power, transmission and distribution costs, but are subject to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Goods_and_Services_Tax_(Canada)" title="Goods and Services Tax (Canada)">Goods and Services Tax</a> (GST) and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quebec_Sales_Tax" title="Quebec Sales Tax">Quebec Sales Tax</a> (QST).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[134]</a></sup> As of April 1, 2012, customers pay 5.32\xc2\xa2/kWh for the first 30 daily kWh, while the remainder is sold at 7.51\xc2\xa2/kWh.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[135]</a></sup> The average monthly bill for a residential customer was approximately C$100 in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[136]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Electric meter readings are usually conducted every two months and bills are bimonthly. However, the company offers an optional <i>Equalized Payment Plan</i> allowing residential customers to pay their annual electricity costs in 12 monthly installments, based on past consumption patterns of the current customer address and the average temperature in that location.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[137]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 2007, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec pulled out of a Canadian government initiative to install <a href="/wiki/Smart_meter" title="Smart meter">smart meters</a> across the province, stating that it would be "too costly to deliver real savings".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[138]</a></sup> Since then, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec organized a 2-year pilot project, involving 2,000 customers in 4 cities, with <a href="/wiki/Net_metering" title="Net metering">time of use metering</a>. A report, filed with the <i>R\xc3\xa9gie de l\'\xc3\xa9nergie</i>, in the summer of 2010 concluded that the effect of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marginal_cost_pricing" title="Marginal cost pricing">marginal cost pricing</a> with three levels of pricing in the winter would lead to minimal load and energy savings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[139]</a></sup> The company intends to gradually phase-in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Advanced_Metering_Infrastructure" title="Advanced Metering Infrastructure">Advanced Metering Infrastructure</a> (AMI) between 2011 and 2017. Early efforts will focus on meter data transfer, connect-disconnect, outage detection and theft reduction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[140]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_customers">Industrial customers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Industrial customers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Usine_Alcan_Laterri%C3%A8re2.JPG"><img alt="A large aluminium smelter." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="1920" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Usine_Alcan_Laterri%C3%A8re2.JPG/220px-Usine_Alcan_Laterri%C3%A8re2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Usine_Alcan_Laterri%C3%A8re2.JPG/330px-Usine_Alcan_Laterri%C3%A8re2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Usine_Alcan_Laterri%C3%A8re2.JPG/440px-Usine_Alcan_Laterri%C3%A8re2.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Usine_Alcan_Laterri%C3%A8re2.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Rio_Tinto_Alcan" title="Rio Tinto Alcan">Rio Tinto Alcan</a>\'s Laterriere smelter in <a href="/wiki/Saguenay,_Quebec" title="Saguenay, Quebec">Saguenay</a>. Large industrial users, especially the metallurgy and the pulp and paper industries, use 40.6% of all electricity sold in Quebec.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>For more than a century, industrial development in Quebec has been stimulated by the abundance of hydroelectric resources. Energy represents a significant expenditure in the pulp and paper and aluminum sectors. two industries with long-standing traditions in Quebec. In 2010, industrial customers purchased 68.4 TWh from Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec, representing 40.4% of all electricity sold by the company on the domestic market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2011a97_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2011a97-144">[141]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Smurfit-Stone_La_Tuque_1.jpg"><img alt="A large paper mill." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Smurfit-Stone_La_Tuque_1.jpg/220px-Smurfit-Stone_La_Tuque_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Smurfit-Stone_La_Tuque_1.jpg/330px-Smurfit-Stone_La_Tuque_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Smurfit-Stone_La_Tuque_1.jpg/440px-Smurfit-Stone_La_Tuque_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Smurfit-Stone_La_Tuque_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe Smurfit-Stone paper mill in <a href="/wiki/La_Tuque,_Quebec" title="La Tuque, Quebec">La Tuque</a>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The Quebec government uses low electricity rates to attract new business and consolidate existing jobs. Despite its statutory obligation to sell electric power to every person who so requests, the province has reserved the right to grant large load allocations to companies on a case by case basis since 1974. The threshold was set at 175 MW from 1987 to 2006<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[142]</a></sup> and was reduced to 50 MW in the government\'s 2006\xe2\x80\x932015 energy strategy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGovernment_of_Quebec200624_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGovernment_of_Quebec200624-146">[143]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Large industrial users pay a lower rate than the domestic and commercial customers, because of lower distribution costs. In 2010, the largest industrial users, the <i>Rate L</i> customers, were paying an average of 4.66\xc2\xa2/kWh whereas companies with special contracts paid 3.07\xc2\xa2/kWh.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[144]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 1987, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec and the Quebec government agreed to a series of controversial deals with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aluminum" title="Aluminum">aluminum</a> giants <a href="/wiki/Alcan" title="Alcan">Alcan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alcoa" title="Alcoa">Alcoa</a>. These risk sharing contracts set the price of electricity based on a series of factors, including aluminum world prices and the value of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_dollar" title="Canadian dollar">Canadian dollar</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[145]</a></sup> Those agreements are gradually being replaced by one based on published rates.</p>\n<p>On May 10, 2007, the Quebec government signed an agreement with Alcan. The agreement, which is still in force despite the company\'s merger with <a href="/wiki/Rio_Tinto_Group" title="Rio Tinto Group">Rio Tinto Group</a>, renews the water rights concession on the Saguenay and Peribonka rivers. In exchange, Alcan has agreed to invest in its Quebec facilities and to maintain jobs and its corporate headquarters in Montreal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[146]</a></sup></p>\n<p>On December 19, 2008, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec and Alcoa signed a similar agreement. This agreement, which expires in 2040, maintains the provision of electricity to Alcoa\'s three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aluminum_smelter" title="Aluminum smelter">aluminum smelters</a> in the province, located in <a href="/wiki/Baie-Comeau" title="Baie-Comeau">Baie-Comeau</a>, <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9cancour,_Quebec" title="B\xc3\xa9cancour, Quebec">B\xc3\xa9cancour</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deschambault-Grondines,_Quebec" title="Deschambault-Grondines, Quebec">Deschambault-Grondines</a>. In addition, the deal will allow Alcoa to modernize the Baie-Comeau plant which will increase its production capacity by 110,000 tonnes a year, to a total of 548,000 tonnes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[147]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Several economists, including <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_Laval" title="Universit\xc3\xa9 Laval">Universit\xc3\xa9 Laval</a>\'s Jean-Thomas Bernard and G\xc3\xa9rard B\xc3\xa9langer, have challenged the government\'s strategy and argue that sales to large industrial customers are very costly to the Quebec economy. In an article published in 2008, the researchers estimate that, under the current regime, a job in a new aluminum smelter or an expansion project costs the province between C$255,357 and C$729,653 a year, when taking into consideration the money that could be made by selling the excess electricity on the New York market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEB.C3.A9langerBernard2008_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEB.C3.A9langerBernard2008-151">[148]</a></sup></p>\n<p>This argument is disputed by large industrial customers, who point out that data from 2000 to 2006 indicate that electricity exports prices get lower when quantities increase, and vice versa. "We find that the more we export, the less lucrative it gets", said Luc Boulanger, the head of the association representing Quebec\'s large industrial customers. In his opinion, the high volatility of electricity markets and the transmission infrastructure physical limitations reduce the quantities of electricity that can be exported when prices are higher.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoulanger2008_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoulanger2008-152">[149]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Export_markets">Export markets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Export markets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable centre" style="text-align:right; width:100%;">\n<caption><b>Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec exports and brokerage activities in Canada and the United States (2002\xe2\x80\x932011)</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012a97_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2012a97-153">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HQ2007_31-3"><a href="#cite_note-HQ2007-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="text-align:right;">90.10</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">82.40</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">79.47</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">95.42</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">75.32</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">85.20</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">63.97</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Christmas_tree_near_the_Quincy_Market.jpg"><img alt="Christmas tree near Boston\'s Quincy Market." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1772" data-file-width="1299" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Christmas_tree_near_the_Quincy_Market.jpg/150px-Christmas_tree_near_the_Quincy_Market.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Christmas_tree_near_the_Quincy_Market.jpg/225px-Christmas_tree_near_the_Quincy_Market.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Christmas_tree_near_the_Quincy_Market.jpg/300px-Christmas_tree_near_the_Quincy_Market.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Christmas_tree_near_the_Quincy_Market.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nPart of the electricity used in <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a> comes from the remote dams in the <a href="/wiki/James_Bay" title="James Bay">James Bay</a> area.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec sells part of its surplus electricity to neighbouring systems in Canada and the United States under long term contracts and transactions on the New England, New York and Ontario <a href="/wiki/Electricity_market#Wholesale_electricity_market" title="Electricity market">bulk energy markets</a>. Two subsidiaries, <i>HQ Energy Marketing</i> and <i>HQ Energy Services (U.S.)</i> are engaged in the electricity trade on behalf of the company. In 2010, export sales of electricity brought in $1,513 million for a transaction volume of 23.3 TWh, despite "exceptionally low runoff", according to the company. Net exports accounted for a net income of $1,034 million and a net reservoir drawdown of 12.5 TWh.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2011a9_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHydro-Qu.C3.A9bec2011a9-156">[152]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Although most export sales are now short-term transactions, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec has entered into long-term export contracts in the past. In 1990, the company signed a 328-MW deal with a group of 13 electric distributors in <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a>. Exports from Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec account for 28% of all power used in the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[153]</a></sup> On March 11, 2010, Vermont\'s two largest utilities, Green Mountain Power and Central Vermont Public Service, entered into a tentative 26-year deal with Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec to purchase up to 225 MW of hydro power from 2012 to 2038. The memorandum of understanding provides for a price smoothing mechanism shielding Vermont customers from market price spikes. The deal is contingent upon the enactment designating large hydro as "renewable energy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[154]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The renewable energy law, H.781,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[155]</a></sup> was adopted by both houses of the legislature and signed into law by governor <a href="/wiki/Jim_Douglas" title="Jim Douglas">Jim Douglas</a> on June 4, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[156]</a></sup></p>\n<p>A second contract has been signed with Cornwall Electric, a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Fortis_Inc." title="Fortis Inc.">Fortis Inc.</a>, a utility serving 23,000 customers in the <a href="/wiki/Cornwall,_Ontario" title="Cornwall, Ontario">Cornwall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a> area. The contract was renewed in 2008 and will be in force until 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[157]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The company has several advantages in its dealings in export markets. First, its costs are not affected by the fluctuations of <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuel</a> prices, since <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">hydropower</a> requires no fuel. Also, Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec has a lot of flexibility in matching supply and demand, so it can sell electricity at higher prices during the day and replenish its reservoirs at night, when wholesale prices are lower. Third, the Quebec power grid peaks in winter because of heating, unlike most neighboring systems, where peak demand occur on very warm days in the summer, due to the <a href="/wiki/Air_conditioning" title="Air conditioning">air conditioning</a> needs of homes and offices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENorth_American_Reliability_Corporation2008138_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENorth_American_Reliability_Corporation2008138-162">[158]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The election of <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>\xe2\x80\x94a supporter of <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> <a href="/wiki/Emissions_trading" title="Emissions trading">emissions trading</a> and the development of <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">electric cars</a>\xe2\x80\x94as <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">president of the United States</a> in <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2008" title="United States presidential election, 2008">2008</a> was seen as a positive development for the company\'s outlook. Despite the success of the previous policy of short-term sales on neighboring energy markets, the Quebec government asked Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec management to write a new strategic plan, focusing on long-term sale agreements with US distributors, as was the case after the commissioning of the James Bay Project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[159]</a></sup> The new plan was released in July 2009.</p>\n<p>Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec crews were also loaned to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Metropolitan_Area" title="New York Metropolitan Area">New York Metropolitan Area</a> following <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Sandy" title="Hurricane Sandy">Hurricane Sandy</a> in October/November 2012.</p>\n<p><br/></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Presidents">Presidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hydro-Qu%C3%A9bec&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit Martel</a></td>\n<td>June 3, 2015</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>From 1944 to 1978, management of Hydro-Qu\xc3\xa9bec consisted of five commissioners, one of them acting as president.</p>\n<h2><span
